<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="km4476_kraft_foods_inc._reports_third_quarter_results"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_km4476_2"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>KRAFT FOODS&nbsp;INC. REPORTS THIRD QUARTER RESULTS    <BR>    </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;NORTHFIELD, IL&#151;October&nbsp;15, 2003&#151;Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. (NYSE: KFT) today reported third quarter 2003 diluted earnings per share of
$0.47, down 6.0% versus 2002. The company reconfirmed its full year 2003 guidance for diluted earnings per share of $2.00-$2.05 and discretionary cash flow growth of 10% plus. The company
also indicated that 2003 full year volume growth from ongoing businesses, which excludes the impact of businesses sold, would be around 1.5%. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"Our
third quarter results reflect a continuation of the challenges we faced in the second quarter," said Roger K. Deromedi, Co-Chief Executive Officer of Kraft Foods.
"Volume growth from ongoing businesses of 1% was below our expectations as solid gains in several North American businesses and Asia Pacific were partially offset by continued weakness in the U.S.
cookie category and the impact of the summer heat wave in Europe on our chocolate and coffee businesses." </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Third
quarter earnings per share declined 6.0%, driven by a decrease in operating income, partly offset by lower interest expense. Operating income was down 9.6%, as higher commodity and
benefit costs, the previously announced investment spending in focus categories, and unfavorable mix, were marginally offset by a gain on sale of the </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>reis-fit</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> rice business in Europe and the effects of
favorable currency. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Gross
profit declined 1.7% as higher commodity costs more than offset the impact of net revenue gains. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues increased 3.7% due to favorable currency of $213&nbsp;million and pricing actions in response to commodity and devaluation-driven cost increases, partly offset by higher
promotional spending, adverse product mix and the impact of divestitures. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
was down 0.2%, partially reflecting the impact of divestitures. Volume growth from ongoing businesses of 1.0% resulted from tack-on acquisitions, which accounted for
0.6&nbsp;percentage points of growth, solid growth in several North American businesses, and broad strength across the Asia Pacific region. Volume was lower in U.S. cookies as the category declined
during the quarter due to several factors, including higher prices, lower impact from new products, and switching to alternate categories. Volume was also lower in Europe, as the summer heat wave
drove double-digit declines in the chocolate markets in France and Germany and mid to high single-digit declines in the coffee markets across key geographies. The company estimates that these
businesses&#151;U.S. cookies and European chocolate and coffee&#151;combined to impact overall volume growth versus the prior year by a full percentage point. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
the third quarter, the company spent approximately $45&nbsp;million of the previously announced investment program, primarily in September. In cheese, cold cuts and crackers, share
and consumption trends showed solid improvement in September. In coffee, third quarter volume met expectations due to strong non-measured channel growth and an improvement in consumption,
while shares declined due to significant competitive activity. In cookies, third quarter share trends improved versus the second quarter, while consumption was soft due to continued category declines. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"The
initial phase of our investment program in focus categories is showing early signs of meeting our objectives," said Betsy D. Holden, Co-Chief Executive Officer of Kraft
Foods. "We are encouraged by our September share and consumption trends in cheese, cold cuts and crackers. However, we have </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>1</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=1,EFW="2120407",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="2",CHK=430342,FOLIO='1',FILE='DISK019:[03CHI6.03CHI4476]KM4476A.;9',USER='MWEINST',CD='15-OCT-2003;13:41' -->
<A NAME="page_km4476_1_2"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>encountered
heightened competitive activity in coffee and continued category softness in cookies. While we believe we have the right programs in place to drive top line growth through consumption and
share trend improvements, we need to see ongoing progress throughout the fourth quarter." </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As
part of the company's strategy to optimize its portfolio, it continues to review certain non-core businesses for potential divestitures, such as the previously announced
sale of the Invernizzi fresh cheese business in Italy. The earnings guidance range in this release does not account for the potential gain or loss on the possible future sale of a business. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
the quarter, the company declared a regular quarterly dividend of $0.18 per common share, a 20% increase versus the prior quarterly dividend, and repurchased 2.4&nbsp;million
shares of Class&nbsp;A common stock for $70&nbsp;million. Additionally, the company issued $1.5&nbsp;billion in long-term notes to refinance maturing short-term debt due
to Altria Group. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Guidance
for 2004 will be provided in January. Previously announced factors impacting the company in 2004 include significantly higher benefit costs, primarily pensions, and a full year
of higher investment spending to enhance brand equity and growth prospects primarily in its focus categories. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>As described in "Note&nbsp;13, Segment Reporting" of Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc.'s 2002 Annual Report, management reviews operating companies income (OCI), which is
defined as operating income before corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this
measure to help investors analyze business performance and trends. (For a reconciliation of OCI to operating income, see the Condensed Statements of Earnings contained in this
release.)</I></FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>KRAFT FOODS NORTH AMERICA  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net revenues for Kraft Foods North America (KFNA) increased 1.9% to $5,326&nbsp;million, as favorable currency of $46&nbsp;million, higher volume and
increased pricing were partially offset by higher promotional spending, including investments to manage price gaps and improve share trends on cheese, cold cuts, coffee and biscuits. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
increased 0.9%. Excluding the impact of a small, divested confectionery business, volume grew 1.0% behind strength in ready-to-drink beverages,
foodservice, Enhancers and meats, partially offset by consumption weakness in select categories, particularly cookies. Third quarter share trends generally improved versus the first half, with pound
share increasing or flat in categories representing about 50% of the OCI from the top 25&nbsp;North American categories. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OCI
decreased 11.6% to $1,152&nbsp;million due to higher commodity and benefit costs, the previously announced investment spending in focus categories and unfavorable mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Following
are the results by segment for KFNA: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Cheese, Meals and Enhancers</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume was up 1.5%, with solid results in Enhancers, Meals, foodservice and Mexico. Net revenues increased
3.7%, driven by currency and volume gains. OCI declined 11.5% to $498&nbsp;million, due primarily to unfavorable commodity and benefit costs and increased promotional spending in Cheese to improve
share trends, partially offset by volume growth and currency. Cheese volume was flat as improving consumption trends, including non-measured channels, were offset by trade inventory
reductions. Increased merchandising drove volume gains in </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Kraft</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> brand dinners, salad dressings and barbecue sauce. Higher shipments to national accounts
drove foodservice volume growth, while new ready-to-drink beverage products drove volume growth in Mexico. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume was down 3.9%, of which 0.7&nbsp;percentage points reflects the impact of the confectionery
divestiture in 2002. The remainder of the decrease was due primarily to lower shipments of cookies. Net revenues declined 2.2% as lower volume and higher promotional </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>2</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=2,EFW="2120407",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="2",CHK=201856,FOLIO='2',FILE='DISK019:[03CHI6.03CHI4476]KM4476A.;9',USER='MWEINST',CD='15-OCT-2003;13:41' -->
<A NAME="page_km4476_1_3"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>spending
more than offset the impact of price increases taken earlier this year on cookies and crackers. OCI was down 19.3% to $230&nbsp;million due to lower volume, higher commodity costs and
increased promotional spending in biscuits to improve share trends, partially offset by pricing and synergy savings. Biscuit volume declined due primarily to continued category weakness in cookies. In
crackers, both consumption and share improved versus prior year, supported by the introduction of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Ritz</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> Chips. In Snacks, shipments increased double
digits as the nuts category benefited from growing consumer recognition of nuts' health benefits. Confectionery volume was also up, led by higher shipments of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Life
Savers</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> candies and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Altoids</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> mints. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Beverages, Desserts and Cereals</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume was up 2.4%. Net revenues increased 2.0%, in-line with shipments. OCI was down 5.2% to
$275&nbsp;million due primarily to higher commodity and benefit expenses and increased marketing spending behind the coffee business, partially offset by stronger shipments. In Beverages, volume
gains were led by continued momentum in ready-to-drink, aided by the launches of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Capri Sun</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> Sport and </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Capri Sun Island Refreshers</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> beverages, as well as by
stronger consumption of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Crystal Light</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> powdered soft
drinks. In Coffee, volume was flat as the impact of heightened competitive activity was offset by strong growth in non-measured channels due to targeted merchandising programs. Desserts
volume was up, led by growth in </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Handi-Snacks</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> shelf stable desserts behind back-to-school merchandising programming, as well as </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Jell-O</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> refrigerated
ready-to-eat desserts and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Balance</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>
nutrition/energy bars, both of which benefited from new products. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Post</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cereal volume was lower due to category and share declines in
ready-to-eat cereal. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Oscar Mayer and Pizza</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume was up 1.8%. Net revenues increased 3.5% due to higher shipments and commodity-driven price increases in
meats. OCI declined 9.7% to $149&nbsp;million due primarily to higher commodity and benefit costs and increased promotional spending in cold cuts to improve share trends, partially offset by higher
shipments. In meats, volume gains were recorded in cold cuts, hot dogs, bacon, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Lunchables</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> lunch combinations and </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Boca</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> meat alternatives. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>3</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=3,EFW="2120407",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="2",CHK=124957,FOLIO='3',FILE='DISK019:[03CHI6.03CHI4476]KM4476A.;9',USER='MWEINST',CD='15-OCT-2003;13:41' -->
<BR>
<!-- THIS IS THE END OF A COMPOSITION COMPONENT -->
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="page_ko4476_1_4"> </A> </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B><I>KRAFT FOODS INTERNATIONAL  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net revenues for Kraft Foods International&nbsp;(KFI) grew 8.2% to $2,154 million, due to currency favorability of $167&nbsp;million. Pricing actions to
offset higher commodity and devaluation-driven cost increases in Latin America and volume growth from the acquisitions of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Kar&nbsp;Gida</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> salted snacks
in Turkey and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Family Nutrition</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> biscuits in Egypt were offset by unfavorable mix and the divestitures of the </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>reis-fit</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> rice business in Europe in 2003 and a
Latin America bakery ingredients business in 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume
decreased 3.2%, driven by the impact of divestitures. Volume from ongoing businesses increased 0.8%, as a 2.5 percentage point impact from acquisitions was largely offset by the
adverse impact of the summer heat wave across Europe on the chocolate and coffee categories and price competition. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OCI
increased 2.3% to $307 million, as the effects of currency favorability of $18&nbsp;million, a gain on sale of the </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>reis-fit</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> business
in Europe of $23&nbsp;million and higher pricing were partially offset by unfavorable mix, higher benefit costs and infrastructure investment in developing markets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Europe, Middle East and Africa (EMEA)</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume decreased 1.4%, impacted by the </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>reis-fit</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>
divestiture in 2003. Ongoing volume was down 0.4%, as acquisitions and growth in Poland, Russia, Romania and Ukraine were more than offset by declines in European chocolate and coffee. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues increased 9.5%, as favorable currency and pricing were partially offset by the volume decline and unfavorable mix. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OCI
increased 1.3% to $238 million, driven by a gain on the sale of the </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>reis-fit</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> business of $23&nbsp;million, favorable currency of
$22&nbsp;million and higher pricing, partly offset by lower volume, higher benefit costs, infrastructure investment in Eastern Europe and costs associated with the previously announced closure of a
Nordic snacks plant. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;EMEA
confectionery and beverage volumes were down reflecting the significant adverse impact of the summer heat wave. In addition, coffee volume was hurt by price competition in Germany.
However, growth was up double-digits in Russia benefiting from expanded distribution of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Maxwell House</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Jacobs</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> coffee, and in Poland behind new products
including </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Jacobs Ice Presso</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> ready-to-drink coffee. EMEA
snacks volume was up, with gains in biscuits and salted snacks, benefiting from acquisitions, more than offsetting the confectionery decline. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;EMEA
convenient meals volume was lower, impacted by the divestiture of the </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>reis-fit</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> business in Europe, but moderated by the good
performance of </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Simmenthal</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> canned meats in Italy. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Latin America and Asia Pacific (LAAP)</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume decreased 5.5%, as the impact of the 2002 divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients
business more than offset volume growth from ongoing businesses of 2.6%, driven by gains across all key markets in Asia Pacific. Latin America volume was below last year, reflecting declines in Brazil
due to economic weakness and trade inventory reductions and Venezuela as a result of a shortage of raw materials due to currency controls, and growth in Argentina. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
revenues increased 4.3%, as pricing and ongoing volume gains were partially offset by a divestiture, and unfavorable currency and mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OCI
increased 6.2% to $69&nbsp;million, with growth from pricing to cover higher devaluation-driven costs, moderated by unfavorable mix, an adverse currency impact of $4&nbsp;million
and the absence of earnings from a divested business. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LAAP
snacks volume was lower, due to economic weakness and trade inventory reductions in Brazil and raw material unavailability in Venezuela, partly offset by new products in Argentina,
Australia and China. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>4</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=4,EFW="2120407",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="2",CHK=222545,FOLIO='4',FILE='DISK019:[03CHI6.03CHI4476]KO4476A.;7',USER='MWEINST',CD='15-OCT-2003;13:43' -->
<A NAME="page_ko4476_1_5"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LAAP
beverages volume grew by double-digits, driven by gains in Brazil, Venezuela and China. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Tang</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> volume grew strongly in China,
benefiting from joint promotions with </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Pacific</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> crackers. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>*

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
company will host a conference call with members of the investment community and media at 5:00&nbsp;p.m. ET on October&nbsp;15, 2003. Access to a live audio webcast of the call
is available at </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>www.kraft.com</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and a replay of the webcast will be available on our web site. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Kraft
Foods Inc. is the largest branded food and beverage company headquartered in the United States and the second largest worldwide. Kraft Foods markets many of the world's leading
food brands, including </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Kraft</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cheese, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Jacobs</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Maxwell
House</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> coffees, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Nabisco</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cookies and crackers, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Philadelphia</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cream cheese, </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Oscar Mayer</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>
meats, </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Post</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> cereals and </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>Milka</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> chocolates, in
more than 150&nbsp;countries. </FONT></P>

pursuant to the Safe Harbor Provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995. The following important factors could cause actual results and outcomes to differ materially from those
contained in such forward-looking statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company is subject to unfavorable currency movements, intense competition, changes in consumer preferences and demand for its products, including publicity concerning the health
implications of obesity and trans fatty acids, changing prices for raw materials, fluctuations in levels of customer inventories and the effects of foreign economies and local economic and market
conditions. The Company's benefit expense is subject to the investment performance of pension plan assets, interest rates and cost increases for medical benefits offered to employees and retirees. The
Company's results are dependent upon its continued ability to promote brand equity successfully; to anticipate and respond to new consumer trends; to develop new products and markets and to broaden
brand portfolios; to compete effectively with lower-priced products in a consolidating environment at the retail and manufacturing levels; to improve productivity; to consummate and successfully
integrate acquisitions, including Nabisco; to maintain access to credit markets; and other risks detailed from time to time in the Company's publicly-filed documents. The Company's results are also
dependent upon its borrowing costs and credit ratings, which may in turn be influenced by the credit ratings of Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. The Company cautions that the foregoing list of important
factors is not exclusive, any forward-looking statement included in this press release is made as of the date of this press release, and the Company does not undertake to update any forward-looking
statement. </FONT></P>
